        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316087841" href="/book/show/7959998-the-poison-throne">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590834-estara?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102467223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4410573735063157276">This epic fantasy series clearly ought not to have been published in three books, as the whole first book is a set-up for the doom to come. The main characters are engaging, especially Wynter and Ravi, with Christopher still something of an enigma. <br/><br/>Although the book is written in third person we only are shown as much as Wynter knows, which means a lot of things are unclear, easy to misunderstand or guess work - like real life if you were in her situation. The information isn't spoon-fed - no Ga</span>
  <span id="freeText4410573735063157276" style="display:none">This epic fantasy series clearly ought not to have been published in three books, as the whole first book is a set-up for the doom to come. The main characters are engaging, especially Wynter and Ravi, with Christopher still something of an enigma. <br /><br />Although the book is written in third person we only are shown as much as Wynter knows, which means a lot of things are unclear, easy to misunderstand or guess work - like real life if you were in her situation. The information isn't spoon-fed - no Gandalf or Elven council - that's why it only makes sense to read this book if you can lay your hands on the following two right away - fortunately not a problem when reading in ebook and all three are already out.<br /><br />Don't read this for a picker-upper, but if you're willing to dive into a court in turmoil right before everything goes down the drain and watching what happens to people on all sides who do what they think is best and have to decide what to sacrifice to protect or reach their aims and no clear-cut villains or even heroes, but characters you can learn to care for then this is a good choice.<br /><br />I hope the next two books give a resolution I can live with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4410573735063157276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1847585259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10655560718021481653">I loved the characters in this, and the fact that I couldn't ever tell where it was going-- not that I felt adrift in it, but just that it didn't follow the formula I've come to expect from alternate history/coming of age novels. I really liked the strong female lead character and her loving, tender relationships with her father and brother. It was nice to have characters whose strength comes from a supportive family rather than damaged characters who have to find their strength on their own-- b</span>
  <span id="freeText10655560718021481653" style="display:none">I loved the characters in this, and the fact that I couldn't ever tell where it was going-- not that I felt adrift in it, but just that it didn't follow the formula I've come to expect from alternate history/coming of age novels. I really liked the strong female lead character and her loving, tender relationships with her father and brother. It was nice to have characters whose strength comes from a supportive family rather than damaged characters who have to find their strength on their own-- both ways are valid ways of being, of course, but I find there are fewer of the former in literature, so I enjoyed reading something fresh.</span>

<div id="review_2188186947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2188186947" />
    <a title="Alicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54897639-alicia"><img alt="Alicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493503495p2/54897639.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2188186947?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia" href="/user/show/54897639-alicia">Alicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54897639-alicia?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188186947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2193150390503567240">Wynter Moorehawke has just returned from the North (yep, it's just as vague as it sounds) to a court with a missing prince, a corrupt king, and an ailing father.<br/><br/>Even after reading 500 pages of this book I still could not tell you much of the plot. It could've been massively condensed, and the pacing was all over the place. Wynter is an okay character but Razi and Christopher were the <i>real</i> interesting and multidimensional characters. <br/><br/>At first I thought the name Wynter was just a trashy fantasy sp</span>
  <span id="freeText2193150390503567240" style="display:none">Wynter Moorehawke has just returned from the North (yep, it's just as vague as it sounds) to a court with a missing prince, a corrupt king, and an ailing father.<br /><br />Even after reading 500 pages of this book I still could not tell you much of the plot. It could've been massively condensed, and the pacing was all over the place. Wynter is an okay character but Razi and Christopher were the <i>real</i> interesting and multidimensional characters. <br /><br />At first I thought the name Wynter was just a trashy fantasy spelling of Winter but it turned out to be legit. I only found vague sources, but it looks like a Middle English spelling of Winter? It's nice that it's sort of historically accurate, but it still doesn't sit well to name your MC Wynter of all things. If it requires outside research from your book to not be something trashy than maybe don't go with it.<br /><br />And the worldbuilding was a mess!! The set up is basically an alternate universe of medieval Europe except with talking cats and ghosts. But surprise surprise, there's still rampant racism and homophobia. The sexism isn't as big a factor, but I'm not surprised, given the author is a white woman. Really though, at one point Wynter pretty directly says that she wouldn't love her brother as much if he were gay (Y I K E S). At what point are talking cats and ghosts believable but a world without blatant racism and homophobia isn't? Plot twist, gay people don't want to read about a homophobic main character, especially if they never change their mind. <br /><br />I was intrigued for the first half of the book, but the second half made me realize how thinly everything was being held together. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2193150390503567240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1135919363056626569" style="display:none">This book was something very different to what I usually read. I was not expecting what I read. Wynter the main character, although mildly frustrating at times, was an amazing and different character. Her relation with the other characters was really intriguing and it kept me reading continuously.<br /> The story starts when Wynter and her father return to their home country. Being sent away by the king - a good friend of Lorcan (her father) - we are not given much information of why but brief mentions of four years of war. Her father is a master carpenter and she follows in her father's footsteps. On her return, she is excited to reunite with her childhood friends - Razi and Albe. However, to her dismay, Albe is not home but Razi is and he has brought home with him a new mysterious young man called Christopher. Wynter immediately takes to disliking him but as her father grows ill and the kingdom is at risk of being destroyed they become very good friends<br />This book is not getting five stars because it was very confusing. The storyline is still very unclear and there are many things I was unsure of. However, Kiernan's writing is amazing and she is incredibly talented to make such a raw and amazing character such as Wynter and her companions.</span>

<div id="review_1881240484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881240484" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6874390-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333404793p2/6874390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1881240484?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/6874390-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316077064" href="/book/show/7302398-the-poison-throne">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1881240484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3187117665747579860">Let me just start by saying, I loved this book! With that overarching opinion out of the way, I can understand why many people would not. If you dislike not fully understanding the world, this is not the story for you. The story feels REALLY confusing because we are dropped into the middle of this huge political minefield that we have no context for. However, it feels really authentic, because our main character Wynter is right along side us, though she has the benefit of understanding the game,</span>
  <span id="freeText3187117665747579860" style="display:none">Let me just start by saying, I loved this book! With that overarching opinion out of the way, I can understand why many people would not. If you dislike not fully understanding the world, this is not the story for you. The story feels REALLY confusing because we are dropped into the middle of this huge political minefield that we have no context for. However, it feels really authentic, because our main character Wynter is right along side us, though she has the benefit of understanding the game, even if she is as lost as we are when it comes to the state of play. So trying to unravel the world and the political minefield is a bit difficult as a reader. <br /><br />Despite not fully understanding what's going on, I couldn't let this book go. Because of the unclear nature of the plot, the characters are almost completely the draw here. The characters are all compelling, and fascinating mysteries, so even when I have no idea what is happening, I am still drawn in, because there is a mystery behind every single character. Wynter and her father return from five years away, and she left when she was like 11, so even the people she thought she knew best have secrets and facets to discover. This is very different than the other stories I have read with political intrigue. The stakes feel higher and all the more real for there being very little happiness - it is not a romanticized version where the political intrigue is a "game" to those involved, with betrayals and secrets and one-upmanship. It is brutal, and there is little to no light at the end of the tunnel and no one really knows why. Also, I liked that though Wynter is the character the story focuses on, she is not really at the center of the political plot itself. It would be unlikely that major power players in any political game would be confiding secrets to a 15 year old girl, and so they don't. It is a refreshing change from our young adult protagonist being the lynchpin in revolutions or generals in uprisings, and instead to having a role they would more likely be occupying. <br /><br />One thing that did bother me is the voice of the narration doesn't seem to commit to a style. Most of the narration is a bit more formal, like what you could expect in a king's court based on popular entertainment (not a lot of contractions, dabbling in more formalized language like "How fare you?", etc), but Wynter often calls her father "Dad" and it is a bit jarring as it doesn't seem to fit, though it is a fantasy world, and no one says the rules there need to be the same.<br /><br />This book definitely sets the stage for the rest of the series - it doesn't really stand on it's own, but I am definitely looking forward to the rest of the series!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3187117665747579860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1533755829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1533755829" />
    <a title="Alex L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47012733-alex-l"><img alt="Alex L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453837323p2/47012733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1533755829?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex L" href="/user/show/47012733-alex-l">Alex L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1533755829&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1533755829" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17020297641382973670">This book really captivates the reader with Wynter, the loveable, but slightly mysterious, heroine, who must travel far from her homeland in medieval Europe in order to stop the Inquisition. Accompanied by her childhood friends, Prince Alberon, and his half-brother, Razi, they must save their beloved hometown from dissolving into complete and utter chaos and destruction. These friends go on a once-in-a-lifetime adventure, and form unbreakable bonds. They display love, caring, and friendship, whe</span>
  <span id="freeText17020297641382973670" style="display:none">This book really captivates the reader with Wynter, the loveable, but slightly mysterious, heroine, who must travel far from her homeland in medieval Europe in order to stop the Inquisition. Accompanied by her childhood friends, Prince Alberon, and his half-brother, Razi, they must save their beloved hometown from dissolving into complete and utter chaos and destruction. These friends go on a once-in-a-lifetime adventure, and form unbreakable bonds. They display love, caring, and friendship, when faced with impending danger and chaos. <br /><br />Wynter did not have it easy. Almost every day, she was faced with difficult decisions and choices that could put herself and her friends in danger if she made the wrong choice. Back in her hometown, there were harsh laws. Anyone who got caught speaking with either a ghost, or a feline, would be tortured and killed. The Inquisition was almost upon them, and that loomed over the three friends like a dark storm cloud. She knew that back home, her fellow citizens depended on her and the half-brothers, to save them. <br /><br />This book would really appeal to readers who crave adventure, mystery, and action. Sometimes, bits and pieces of the story are shrouded in mystery, making you wonder what could possibly happen next. For those who like adventure stories with a romantic subplot, this is also the book for you, for Christopher and Wynter happen to fall in love. If you do not enjoy cliffhangers, this may not be the right book for you. Overall, I highly recommend this book to readers over the age of 13, for it does include some very serious topics in the plot. <br /><br />Other reviewers felt one of two ways, they loved the main characters, and they thought that Wynter was a very loveable and heroic character. Others had mixed opinions on Wynter. Those who did not like her said that she acted too "moody" and "needy" at the beginning of the story. Others did not approve of the inclusion of the romance between Christopher and Wynter. I agree that Wynter is not perfect, she is a flawed character in many ways, but most of the time she was a hero and tried to do the right thing whenever it was possible. <br /><br />In conclusion, this book was very well written, a great, interesting plot that will captivate the reader into wanting to continue and finish the book. It will have the reader hooked onto every word.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17020297641382973670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1773343288" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773343288" />
    <a title="Kinsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50022402-kinsey"><img alt="Kinsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578083217p2/50022402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1773343288?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kinsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kinsey" href="/user/show/50022402-kinsey">Kinsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316077064" href="/book/show/7302398-the-poison-throne">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773343288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4933172031542580272">Oh, man. Where to even begin?<br/><br/>I picked up the entire Moorehawke trilogy at a book sale for $1.50 and I am so happy I did not pay cover price for them. The entirety of The Poison Throne felt like a prologue that just kept going on for 475 pages. Kiernan completely disregarded the number one rule of writing: each book in a series should be able to stand alone. Beginning. Middle. End. This book, however, did little except explain a basic premise, introduce some characters, and never progressed to an</span>
  <span id="freeText4933172031542580272" style="display:none">Oh, man. Where to even begin?<br /><br />I picked up the entire Moorehawke trilogy at a book sale for $1.50 and I am so happy I did not pay cover price for them. The entirety of The Poison Throne felt like a prologue that just kept going on for 475 pages. Kiernan completely disregarded the number one rule of writing: each book in a series should be able to stand alone. Beginning. Middle. End. This book, however, did little except explain a basic premise, introduce some characters, and never progressed to an actual story-line until the last 50 or so pages.<br /><br />The style of writing just...exhausted me. So much time was spent describing emotions or useless details or trivia I came to think of as "Things Wynter Thinks You Shouldn't Do In Court" that you could honestly skip entire pages at a time and find that nothing had changed. No one, and I do mean *no one*, is capable of bursting into tears or flying into rages as much as the characters in this book do. The obsessive detailing of every single changing expression on every single person's face in every single scene probably added a good 100 pages to the book by itself. Character development was largely non-existent and the main group spent all their time being emotionally devastated by events instead of trying to fight back and/or influence them.<br /><br />Can I also bring up the fact that - in a book about a land with TALKING CATS AND GHOSTS - the main point of contention of Razi becoming heir is because he is "Arab" and not because he is a bastard? The rehashing of the Christian vs. Muslim trope has been played to death and, to be completely honest, Kiernan should leave it to better writers than herself. <br /><br />Also, that part when the characters learn the court is spreading rumors that Razi and Christopher are lovers and Razi flies into a fit and Wynter thinks, and I quote, "I would think differently of him" if he were gay? Docked this book an entire star for me.<br /><br />Will I read the next book in the series? Unfortunately, yes. I find myself reluctantly interested in what Alberon has to say for himself and what The Machine is and whether Jonathan will get dethroned. However, I fear that the next book will be nothing more than a placeholder for the last book in the series, much the same way that the first 400 pages of this book was just a prologue for the next one...</span>
  <a data-text-id="4933172031542580272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_90768265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90768265" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/763559-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277400707p2/763559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90768265?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/763559-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781741758689" href="/book/show/6730664-the-poison-throne">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90768265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7165311470751737147">I really wanted to love this book. Not just because it sounded like the sort of book I should love--mystery, intrigue, romance, adventure--but because I picked it up in New Zealand, several months before it would even come out in the US. And while I usually depend on other people's recommendations for my reading selections, it would be nice, for once, to be on the cutting edge, to discover a gem before everyone else and be the one doing the recommending.<br/><br/>The Poison Throne was decent. Its setting </span>
  <span id="freeText7165311470751737147" style="display:none">I really wanted to love this book. Not just because it sounded like the sort of book I should love--mystery, intrigue, romance, adventure--but because I picked it up in New Zealand, several months before it would even come out in the US. And while I usually depend on other people's recommendations for my reading selections, it would be nice, for once, to be on the cutting edge, to discover a gem before everyone else and be the one doing the recommending.<br /><br />The Poison Throne was decent. Its setting was exquisitely realized, a faux-European kingdom of the middle ages with a realistic feel that I haven't often seen. The characters are deep and intriguing. And there is a promise of mystery and profound happenings.<br /><br />And that's where the book falls flat. For that's all the promise ever is--a promise. Wynter Moorhawke, our intrepid heroine, returns home after a five year absence, to discover that something is <i>not right</i> with the kingdom. We see a lot of what is wrong, but we never really learn <i>why</i> things have changed so much; for that matter, we never really learn the circumstances under which the king sent Wynter and her Father away in the first place, except in the way of the most roundabout and vague hints. <br /><br />And so, while the characters go through trying times and make difficult choices, I was never entirely sure what their motives or reasoning were. It was too clear that there were things <i>they</i> knew that <i>I</i> did not. (Or else they blithely ignored the questions that any rational person <i>should</i> have been asking in their situation.) It kept me from being as involved as I should have been and, even though I enjoyed my reading of the story, by the end I was left asking: what was the point? This is the first in a trilogy; I can only hope that the later books fill in everything that was missing here. But even if they do, it leaves this first installment wanting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7165311470751737147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137469380" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137469380" />
    <a title="Allison (The Allure of Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books"><img alt="Allison (The Allure of Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1247775031p2/1637878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137469380?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison (The Allure of Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison (The Allure of Books)" href="/user/show/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books">Allison (The Allure of Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=other-adult-fantasy">other-adult-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137469380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13073420785948887960">The three books of the series are The Poison Throne, The Crowded Shadows and The Rebel Prince. I'm reviewing them together partly because it would be hard to write individual reviews without a ton of spoilers...but also because I was insanely addicted to the series and read all three books in a row, and in a ridiculously short amount of time. Oh - and fair warning - there will be gushing to follow.<br/><br/>Here, friends. Here is a series to get lost in. This world, these people...they don't let you keep </span>
  <span id="freeText13073420785948887960" style="display:none">The three books of the series are The Poison Throne, The Crowded Shadows and The Rebel Prince. I'm reviewing them together partly because it would be hard to write individual reviews without a ton of spoilers...but also because I was insanely addicted to the series and read all three books in a row, and in a ridiculously short amount of time. Oh - and fair warning - there will be gushing to follow.<br /><br />Here, friends. Here is a series to get lost in. This world, these people...they don't let you keep them on the pages of the book for long. I got so completely caught up in the adventures of Wynter, Razi and Christopher; when I would set the books down for something it would take me a disorienting moment to remember that I wasn't actually with them and part of the story. That, my friends, is the biggest gift a book can give you. <br /><br />The politics, characters and different tribes and nations of people are all so layered and complex. I'm already looking forward to rereading the series sometime in the future because I know there is enough to the story that I will be picking up all kinds of things that I missed the first time. <br /><br /><br />I could never critique these books by saying "I didn't like what this character did in this situation" or "I wish she had written this part different" because...of course there are things I wish the characters hadn't done, or things that I wish had happened differently. Reading these books means watching a world unfold. (I did warn you there'd be gushing.) But, fair warning, there is a lot of intensity, and a lot of things that are hard to read (like human sacrifice).<br /><br />In a lot of ways, reading is a never-ending search for books like these...the ones that give you a complete escape. If you like that feeling (and you know the one I'm talking about), then this really is a trilogy you shouldn't miss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13073420785948887960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1276384024" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1276384024" />
    <a title="Maddy Lanslots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42625743-maddy-lanslots"><img alt="Maddy Lanslots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430330265p2/42625743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1276384024?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddy Lanslots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddy Lanslots" href="/user/show/42625743-maddy-lanslots">Maddy Lanslots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42625743-maddy-lanslots?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42625743-maddy-lanslots?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1276384024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17882176792374588840">It's been a long time since I last re-read this trilogy and I find that the older I get, the more I can appreciate it, because things I didn't fully get before seem to fall into place now. I first discovered the Moorehawke Trilogy in Dutch in the library when I was a young teenager, but back then, I didn't entirely understand all the intrigues of court life in medieval ages. With a much better grasp of that now, these books only got better.<br/><br/>Wynter is a sympathetic main character: she's fifteen ye</span>
  <span id="freeText17882176792374588840" style="display:none">It's been a long time since I last re-read this trilogy and I find that the older I get, the more I can appreciate it, because things I didn't fully get before seem to fall into place now. I first discovered the Moorehawke Trilogy in Dutch in the library when I was a young teenager, but back then, I didn't entirely understand all the intrigues of court life in medieval ages. With a much better grasp of that now, these books only got better.<br /><br />Wynter is a sympathetic main character: she's fifteen years old, but in this setting, that basically makes her a woman already. She still clings to some childhood dreams and memories, but quickly realises that things have changed while she was up north with her father and she has to adjust accordingly. She's clever, strong, and kind, but also clearly still a girl, which is why she's realistic and easy to relate to in her struggles.<br /><br />Balancing her out are the strength of her father, Lorcan, even though he is very ill and insists she stand on her own two feet; and Razi, the royal prince whom she considers her big brother. The two of them, along with newcomer Christopher, are the perfect group of people to be surrounding Wynter as she struggles her way through court life and is faced with difficult decisions. Each character is fleshed out very nicely, despite the fact that the story is entirely written from Wynter's perspective (yet in third-person POV), and you just can't help rooting for them all.<br /><br />If you love medieval fantasy with a refreshing female protagonist, some romance to swoon at, and lots of intrigue and mystery - just like me - then this is the right book trilogy for you. I, at least, am still a fan after all these years, and probably always will be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17882176792374588840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IsGcbp7HA6Ry3UY1Hq5qsrPXtNLFHBic0SwHNnYbXVreXNJT3qXNmyKLTODEfil7DnAr0FAfDfOjXji4eOeh9Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('51LP5Y3Zzrie+CT8/yK0m+5EI1dKmmh8mta0UU4ceJQbz4HYzbsAh86uLikl8vdSU+O8Vd+ZfRPopIvfQOCEOw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17076330932968842746">Celine Kiernan is an award-winning author of fantasy novels for young adults. Her critically acclaimed work combines fantasy elements with the exploration of political, humanitarian and philosophical themes. She is best known for The Moorehawke Trilogy, a dark, complex trilogy of fantasy YA books set in an alternative renaissance Europe. First published in Celine’s native Ireland in 2008, the tril</span>
  <span id="freeText17076330932968842746" style="display:none">Celine Kiernan is an award-winning author of fantasy novels for young adults. Her critically acclaimed work combines fantasy elements with the exploration of political, humanitarian and philosophical themes. She is best known for The Moorehawke Trilogy, a dark, complex trilogy of fantasy YA books set in an alternative renaissance Europe. First published in Celine’s native Ireland in 2008, the trilogy has since been published in 15 different territories, and translated into 10 different languages. In 2009 the first book of the Moorehawke Trilogy, The Poison Throne, won The Readers’ Association of Ireland Award for best book; it was included in the White Raven Collection and short listed for the 2009 Irish Book Awards in two categories (Best Newcomer and Best Children’s Book senior category). In 2010 it was long-listed for an Australian Silver Inky Award.<br /><br />Celine’s fourth novel, Into the Grey (aka Taken Away) – a YA ghost story set in 1970′s Ireland – won the 2012 CBI Book of the Year (formerly The Bisto award) and the CBI Children’s Choice Award. It is the first book to have won both categories. It won the RAI Book of the Year 2013, and has been shortlisted for the Sakura Medal (English High) 2014. In 2013 the Irish Times named it as one of the best children's books of the past 25 years.<br /><br />Born in Dublin, Ireland, 1967, Celine has spent the majority of her working life in the film business, and her career as a classical feature character animator spanned over seventeen years, before she became a full-time writer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17076330932968842746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Speaking on the challenges presented by The Moorehawke Trilogy to the YA reader)<br /><br />You can't choose any of these characters and say, 'Yes! They may not want to. They may have no choice. But they will let you down.&rdquo;</span>
